# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

Perfect! I've compiled a comprehensive analysis of the Kafka consumer group coordinator's state machine. Here's what I found:

## Summary

I identified **14 key Java source files** implementing the consumer group coordinator's state machine in apache/kafka:

### **Classic Group State Machine** (Primary Implementation)
- **ClassicGroupState.java** - Defines the main state enum with 5 states: EMPTY, PREPARING_REBALANCE, COMPLETING_REBALANCE, STABLE, DEAD
- **ClassicGroup.java** - Implements group-level state management with the `transitionTo()` method that enforces valid state transitions
- **ClassicGroupMember.java** - Tracks member-level join/sync states via `awaitingJoinFuture` and `awaitingSyncFuture`

### **State Transition Handlers**
- **GroupMetadataManager.java** - Contains the core orchestration:
  - `classicGroupJoin()` - Processes join requests and transitions group to PREPARING_REBALANCE
  - `classicGroupSync()` - Processes sync requests and transitions to COMPLETING_REBALANCE → STABLE
  - Helper methods: `addMemberThenRebalanceOrCompleteJoin()`, `maybePrepareRebalanceOrCompleteJoin()`

### **Modern Group State Machines**
- **ConsumerGroup.java** - Modern consumer protocol with states: EMPTY, ASSIGNING, RECONCILING, STABLE, DEAD
- **MemberState.java** (modern & streams) - Member-level states like STABLE, UNRELEASED_PARTITIONS, UNREVOKED_PARTITIONS, JOINING
- **ShareGroup.java**, **StreamsGroup.java** - Protocol-specific implementations with their own state enums

The state machine enforces **valid transitions** through the `validPreviousStates` set, ensuring groups follow the rebalancing protocol: **Join Phase (PREPARING_REBALANCE) → Sync Phase (COMPLETING_REBALANCE) → Stable Operation (STABLE)**.

DEAD is a final state before group metadata is cleaned up, so there are no transitions\\n104:      */\\n105:     DEAD(\\\"Dead\\\");\\n106: \\n107:     private final String name;\\n108:     private STABLE.addValidPreviousStates(COMPLETING_REBALANCE);\\n116:         DEAD.addValidPreviousStates(STABLE, PREPARING_REBALANCE, COMPLETING_REBALANCE, EMPTY, DEAD);\\n117:     }\\n118: \\n119:     ClassicGroupState(String name) {\\n120:         this.name = name;\\n121:         this.lowerCaseName = name.toLowerCase(Locale.ROOT);\\n122:     }\\n123: \\n124:     @Override\\n125:     public String consumer group coordinator implements a state machine for managing group membership and rebalancing. The implementation is split between Classic groups (traditional protocol) and Modern groups (consumer protocol, share protocol, and streams protocol).\\n\\n**Classic Group State Machine:**\\nThe core state machine is defined in `ClassicGroupState.java` (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/classic/) with five states:\\n1. EMPTY - Group has no members, waiting for new members to join\\n2. PREPARING_REBALANCE - Group is in the join phase, collecting join requests from members\\n3. COMPLETING_REBALANCE - Group is in the sync phase, awaiting assignments from the leader\\n4. STABLE - All members have joined and synced, group is operational\\n5. DEAD - Group metadata is being removed\\n\\nThe valid state transitions are enforced through the `validPreviousStates` set in `ClassicGroupState`, defining the valid transitions:\\n- EMPTY \u2192 PREPARING_REBALANCE\\n- PREPARING_REBALANCE \u2192 COMPLETING_REBALANCE or EMPTY\\n- COMPLETING_REBALANCE \u2192 STABLE\\n- STABLE/PREPARING_REBALANCE/COMPLETING_REBALANCE/EMPTY \u2192 DEAD\\n\\n**Join Phase Implementation:**\\nMember join state is tracked in `ClassicGroupMember.java` with methods `isAwaitingJoin()` which checks if `awaitingJoinFuture` is set. When members send join requests, the `classicGroupJoin()` method in `GroupMetadataManager.java` processes them and manages the group's transition to PREPARING_REBALANCE. The flow calls `addMemberThenRebalanceOrCompleteJoin()` and `maybePrepareRebalanceOrCompleteJoin()` to coordinate the state transitions.\\n\\n**Sync Phase Implementation:**\\nMember sync state is tracked with `isAwaitingSync()` checking if `awaitingSyncFuture` is set. The `classicGroupSync()` method in `GroupMetadataManager.java` handles sync requests from members. Once all members have synced with their assignments, the group transitions from COMPLETING_REBALANCE to STABLE.\\n\\n**State Transitions:**\\nState transitions are managed through the `transitionTo()` method in `ClassicGroup.java`, which enforces valid transitions and tracks both current and previous states. Invalid transitions throw an `IllegalStateException`.\\n\\n**Modern Groups:**\\nModern consumer groups (`ConsumerGroup.java` in modern/consumer/) implement their own state machine with states: EMPTY, ASSIGNING, RECONCILING, STABLE, DEAD. Member states are defined in `MemberState.java` (modern/) with states like STABLE, UNRELEASED_PARTITIONS, UNREVOKED_PARTITIONS, JOINING. Similar patterns are implemented for ShareGroups (`ShareGroup.java`) and StreamsGroups (`StreamsGroup.java`), each with their own state enums and member state tracking.\\n\\nThe coordinator service (`GroupCoordinatorService.java`) and main coordinator (`GroupCoordinator.java`) orchestrate these state machines by routing join and sync requests to the appropriate handlers in `GroupMetadataManager.java`, which then manages the group state transitions based on member responses and timeout conditions.\"\n}\n",
